<Text>I took a group of friends (not from the Bay Area) to Bootie last night (2-20-10) and we had a blast. We arrived a little before 1am. There was no line and the cover was $12. The music was great and we danced until 3am! I love the music and I love the layout of the club. There is a second floor where you can view the whole dance floor from above and a separate room that played trance type music. There are side boxes that allowed people (girls and guys) dance on and the stage area was open for everyone to dance on, which I thought was very fun as well. Over all my friends and I had a great time and really enjoyed the music. The only negative thing I can say is that the bathroom was very dirty. I know it is hard to maintain but there was water (at least I hope it was water) all over the floor.< /Text>< pics>

<text>As someone who decided to go to CrossFit ATR because of its superb ratings online, I wanted to confirm that it not only meets the hype; but vastly exceeds it. When I first started training at CrossFit ATR, one of my primary concerns was the safety of the movements we'd be doing; especially because most of them were new to me. After training at CrossFit ATR for three years, I can confidently say that the coaches always stress the importance of safety and go-over each movement step-by-step at the beginning of class. Furthermore, the coaches at ATR carefully watch each class and will help correct any issues with an athlete who may be struggling with a movement. Beyond CrossFit ATR''s prioritization of safety, the coaches are fantastic individuals who truly care about their members and want the individual to achieve their goals just as badly as the member does. The other thing that I love about CrossFit ATR is how accessible and scalable it is for everyone. The members of the gym range from all ages and walks of life; and the workouts can be structured and scaled to meet each participant's difficulty level. I've never once been forced to complete a workout that made me feel uncomfortable or one that I thought was dangerous. Outside of the training aspect of CrossFit ATR the community here is fantastic. I've made several friends during my time at CrossFit ATR and there are social events that occur outside the gym approximately once every two months.

There are so many other positives that I could go on and on about in regards to CrossFit ATR, so I thought it might be easier to create a list summarizing the highlights:

- Passionate coaches that truly care about their members
- Safety is a priority
- Flexible class times that can meet your schedule (3 classes in the morning, one at noon, and 4 classes in the afternoon)
- Olympic lifting classes on Thursday nights and Sunday morning (at no extra charge)
- Powerlifting classes coaching and classes on Monday nights
- Top of the line facility with plenty of space and equipment for each member
- Workouts that vary every single day that are completely scalable to meet the difficulty needs of each member
- Outstanding community that day-by-day feels more like a family
- Parking is never an issue
- Five bathrooms and showers
- The gym uses an application called Wodify to track the performance of each athlete

All in all there isn't enough I can say about CrossFit ATR, other than to come and try it for yourself and smash your athletic goals.</text>< Pictures>

When my last CrossFit gym shut down, it took me a while to find another gym to join. I went to several different CrossFit gyms and none compared to ATR. After my first drop in class I knew right away I was ready to sign up and become a member.

<Rating>5</Rating><Review>Sadly I had to move away from my old gym as the commute was murdering me, so I had to find a gym that better aligned with my schedule and that still  met my standards (which were high ‚Äì CF Humanity). I had explored different options, but ultimately chose ATR. One year later it‚Äôs the right one. Finding a gym is an exploratory process, so definitely check it out.

Coaching:
All the coaches here are extremely attentive. Unlike other places, these coaches aren‚Äôt deep in conversation while coaching. They are Hawkeyes of everyone‚Äôs movement patterns. It is because of this attentiveness, that got me out of my back problems. The head coach, Tom helped me relearn my movements, assign accessory work, and really had me dialed intra-workout. Due to that, my numbers have been growing (and wodify has data to show). Shout out to Arturo for constantly breaking down the Oly lifts for continuous improvement, Claudia for always making sure my body positions are correct and not making bad habits! Steph and Sean for always getting me through the workouts while focusing on my own abilities! Kim, getting me healthy on the nutrition side with great recipes. I can't say enough about the coaches, they have really changed my workout life - and best of all, data is there to prove it!

Programming:
I'd say the program structure is like other gyms - Strength section followed by a metcon ‚Äì with metcon/heros sprinkled in. during the class movements and intents are explained in detail.  In true CF fashion, things are variable, and different muscles groups are worked on. One thing I do notice is that is that it feels like we lift heavier- combined with the great coaching and attentiveness I've been seeing great progress.
There is also other classes such as Power lifting, and Oly Lifting
Last thing about programming id like to mention are the Warm ups. They are thorough and thoughtful in order to get the muscles that we are training that day to warm up. They aren't mini-wods, they are combination of banded movements, Calisthenics, and Mobility, to really prepare you - and honestly I think that has help prevent injuries as well. Also for habitually late people like me, the warm up is on your own at the start of the hour ‚Äì so it gives me flexibility.
The data is in the wodify pudding, the programming works and we have numbers to show for it.

Facilities:
Its a huge gym, I thought my last gym was big, but this place is even larger, with plenty of evening parking, but can get tough during the day with other businesses near by.  There quite a few platforms and racks all with their own set of rings and GHDs. there are plenty of Rowers and Assault bikes.  there are also 4 dedicated oly platforms, racks and bars. There have been times where the classes are busy enough that people must pair up, but its not all the time (and its never been a problem). The weights are neatly organized and labeled. Like most CF gyms, It is a warehouse style setting, and its not some designer looking gym, but who really cares.

People:
Like all great gyms, this place fosters all shapes and sizes. But undoubtedly, everyone is strong, friendly, and helpful. There is great friendly banter between the people that are closer, but i have no doubts you'll find new friends and workout partners. There is also a community forum, and Social media presence (thanks India!) that have helped members with different events outside of gym things. For example, they re-posted my cancer fundraiser!

I've thoroughly enjoyed my time here and will continue to do so. What is critical is that I am getting my fitness in, making great improvements without forming bad habits, and working with great people while having fun! If those are your requirements, then do not pass up ATR. 5 stars.< /Review>< Pictures>

If you are searching for a CrossFit gym in San Diego, look no further than CrossFit ATR. <Text>Nice, helpful staff, big portions, cheap prices and clean interior - what more can a diner ask for in a place like this?
Well, they're is a lot we could ask for, and with what's on offer nowadays, cheap and big doesn't always cut it for a food business.
My chicken Caesar salad was a sizeable portion and filled me for lunch but here's the breakdown: lettuce was a fresh green color without any brown on the edges - a great start. The chicken was well done, in fact a bit too well as only a couple of the bites were nice and tender and the rest was somewhat overcooked. Still tasty and seasoned good, so fine for now. Dressing tasted like the generic store bought stuff that could be whatever you call it, in this case Caesar dressing. The croutons were out of a plastic bag with no expiration date to be sure. They remained at the end of the plate, joined by the brown, pre-bruised avocado. There were some pieces of tomato - one of those rubbery Romas that are used mainly for decoration. Tasted exactly like...nothing.
The final touch (should we call it the coup de gr√¢ce) was the "parmesan" dusting on top. Because of those more sensitive readers I won't describe the flavor of that condiment.
OK, I'm being a bit harsh here, the salad was well edible and with small exceptions I almost finished it. My point is that when you eat out, you'd expect for some additional steps to be taken toward your gastronomical satisfaction. Nothing here showed that this was even attempted, thus my disappointment. I just feel let down and sometimes even insulted in such cases but enough of my whining and let's go find a better place to eat dinner ;)</Text>< name>

<name>Spencer Hom</name><Time>1531107223431</Time>< Rate>
4< /Rate>
< review>
Pretty much a mirror image of the OG Kono's, but just away from the beach. There's indoor and outdoor seating, with the same menu of breakfast and lunch items. An early Sunday brought a small crowd, but it wasn't overwhelming. Ordering was quick, and the food came out in less than 10 minutes.

I got the french toast/bacon/eggs, which is a good portion for a breakfast...I've gotten the big breakfast before and that could be too much. The french toast was cooked well, and it had it's share of flavor...the eggs were cooked right, and the bacon crispy but still had tough parts to chew.

Overall, I recommend it here for a yummy breakfast, just without the view.< /review>

< Text>
Napa needs a restaurant like this! Dim sum was delicious, Spicy Sichuan fish was sufficiently spicy but not numbing. Wow definitely love to try more dishes.

As they are still quite new, I hope they would take some guidance from Chinese restaurateurs on how dishes should be serve, bowls vs plates, soup spoons, chopsticks etc. Waiters are totally clueless on what to put on the table. <text>We go to Napa a few times a years, this time we tried the new Empress M and Single Thread, the last Michelin Star restaurant to try in Napa, plus our usual Buchon and Oxbow public market. To survive the foodies assault in Napa, and stand up against all the top restaurants in Napa is no easy task, and EM has undeniably staked her place as the upscale authentic Chinese restaurant in Napa and got us to return again before we left Napa. The food, whether dim sum, with lots of varieties, or banquet style abalone, by their Michelin Guide chef, is first class. The long and complete wine list includes even Screaming Eagle. The decors of E M are exquisite. The huge courtyard with an authentic gazebo reminds me of the traditional courtyards in China. It even has live performances on Fridays. Although the service side is still rough on the edges, return we shall.< /text>< pics>

<rating>3</rating>< Review>
I would give this place 4-5 for the food, which was a really welcome treat in Napa. Dim Sum was great (although potstickers cold), calamari awesome, spicy fish, mapo tofu, yum, I‚Äôll go back for the food. But the service and experience is weird, like the owner is not around.

Our actual waiter was great, but the rest of staff has no idea what they are doing. Weirdly, they don‚Äôt set the tables and we were served dim sum potstickers like two seconds after we ordered (preprepared?) with no chopsticks or dipping sauce, just sitting there.  Server (not our waiter) just dropped it.  How do we eat it?! And it was not hot.

Then they showed up with an entree (mapo tofu) before we had been served our other dim sum and appetizers! And no plates. Just dump and run.

And also weird was the room.  It‚Äôs a very nice sit down tablecloth dining room, they clearly put in effort and money, but they had Amazon boxes piled on one table and the table next to us had a box of take out containers sitting next to them on the floor. Very sloppy.  And the take out window is in the middle of the dining room. So take out flying by and outside all the time.

They put a lot of effort into this dining room, it‚Äôs very nice and great crowd, but then why have tables not set and boxes everywhere? Where is the owner seeing he is wasting that effort and money if he does not follow through? It‚Äôs like they are still in COVID take out mode and not ready for a formal sit down crowd.

I will go back. It‚Äôs the best Asian food I have had in Napa.  But I really hope they work on service and get the room ready.  They need Gordon Ramsey for that.<//Review>

I'm planning on dining at Empress M this evening with friends and am looking forward to it.  I'll post my thoughts afterwards.  When I am planning to visit a Napa restaurant, I always like to visit their website and review their offerings in the quiet of my home rather that the busy restaurant with a waiter standing by.  Empress M had a good menu online but no mention at all about any alcohol.  Four diners mentioned beer in passing but that is all I can find.  Do they have a full bar?  Beer?  Wine?  Chinese treats? Like many diners, wine or other libation with or before my meal is almost required.  Wish I knew.  Anyway.  We'll find out .. I'm excited.  (Five stars for now.  We'll see)

<UserId.>115777840836394986577< /UserId.><name>John Lovell<//name><Time>1576382713867< /Time><rate>3< /rate><review>Pros:

-Very large and polished looking showroom. If you are a fan of the Specialized brand and willing to pay top dollar, then you will probably love this shop.
-Convenience: They are open a little later than most bike shops and located in Downtown San Mateo, close to Caltrain. They are great if you are a commuter who needs an accessory or a minor repair done in a pinch.
-Staff is friendly, knowledgeable, and happy to take your questions. They don't use aggressive sales tactics and are honest when it comes to your bike's maintenance needs.

Cons:

Pricing and limited brands: thier very large showroom is almost exclusively dedicated to Specialized, which is known for its products at the high end of the market. You can buy an entry or mid level bicycle from Specialized too, but you will mostly be paying for the prestige of the brand. For budget conscious cyclists who are shopping for bikes at low and middle price points you can get better bikes from most of the other major American bicycle brands (as long as you don't shop for bikes in department stores). Unless you are a big fan of Specialized and have deep pockets, I would recommend buying your bikes from elsewhere.

Maintenance: thier maintenance prices are especially expensive and have only gone up since Talbot's cyclery closed, around the corner. They quoted me $320 for an overhaul tune of my Specialized Crosatrail, (which I use as my beater). That convenience I mentioned earlier does come at a cost. Maybe if you don't want to leave your S-Works in the hands of just any bike shop you should get your bike worked on here. But if your ride is a little less premium there are plenty of bike shops in the area that do great work for prices that are far more reasonable. Also, while they have done minor repairs for me on the spot without an appointment, anything more than minor does tend to take a little longer.</review><Pictures>None<//Pictures>< resp>

104237894128915302628</userid>
<Time>1479922338223<//Time>< review>
I've been here twice since I live down the street.
First, the good: Great burgers, and the Carneros Benedict is delicious. Friendly service for the most part. Kid-friendly menu available and happy to accomodate special requests. The location is slightly off the beaten track for locals, but it's worth checking out when you're tired of Hopmonk and want to go someplace nicer than The Palms or Black Bear Diner.
Now the bad: the portions are small for the prices for some dishes and both times I arrived, I was left standing around for nearly ten minutes when the place was practically empty, even when I had a reservation! They don't seem to have enough staff and no host or hostess for lunch service. The lunch menu ends at 2, when they offer the limited 2-5PM menu and only seat you at banquettes or outside, so don't leave it too late for lunch.
TL;DR - On the whole, it was a pleasant dining experience both times I went and much better than the typical hotel restaurant.  Locals should give it a try!<//review>

This was the first place we ate in Sonoma and we probably could have eaten every meal here. It was very good, from the service to the atmosphere, to the dishes we were served, it made all 6 of the people in our group very happy and very excited for the days to come in Sonoma. I had the steak frites which were excellent, it didn't hurt that the frites were covered in truffle oil which forced me to share them with the table. And the butternut squash soup was some of the best I've had anywhere. Unfortunately, it is sometimes hard to get this restaurant on the phone - but don't give up its worth the ordeal to get such a good meal.<//Review>

< review>
Similar food quality, customer service is comparable to other local McDonald's, close to Home Depot and the El Cerrito BART station; however this McDonald's is kind of small and has a horrible entry/exit layout for the parking lot and drive-thru.

For example, if you enter from Wall Avenue (northbound) San Pablo Avenue from El Cerrito, you are then forced to park (and there are few parking spaces) and you will have no access to the drive-thru (stupid!!!).  Unless you continue going down San Pablo Avenue past the McDonald's, U-turn at the Red Onion/Home Depot Entry, you will then have access to their drive-thru, where a few times I have entered from Wall Avenue and I instantly felt like a circle jerk at this McDonald's.</review>
